  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ed7cdf30-01fa-4c16-9702-46dcf6d8763b'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    Why have you said this on both books, get over it. Saying no offense does not magically make your words nice.<br /><br />I like Gabriel a lot better then that whi<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    Why have you said this on both books, get over it. Saying no offense does not magically make your words nice.<br /><br />I like Gabriel a lot better then that whiny little Witch who couldn't even stand up against her brother. She let the person she so called like, get carved up like a thanksgiving Turkey and doesn't even appear to know about it or at least feel some shred of sorrow.<br /><br />So, who cares. By the author it will be a one sided puppy love from Gabriele's side and Nathan will die broken bleeding defending the so called love of his life no doubt leaving her pregnant or some such thing.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>

<div id="review_869851053" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/869851053" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/869851053?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=paranormal-uf">paranormal-uf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer869851053" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15424190177935277438"><b>The magic is gone.</b><br/><br/>This is not the sequel I had hoped for when I closed <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18079804.Half_Bad__Half_Bad___1_' title='Half Bad (Half Bad, #1) by Sally Green' rel='nofollow noopener'>Half Bad</a> last year, exhilarated and excited for the next installment. I'm going to be completely honest and say I found myself skim-reading parts of the second half because it just could not hold my attention. So if you do happen to read this and discover something amazing, it's possible that it happened while I was busy not caring.<br/><br/>Okay. What went wrong?<br/><br/><b>We started off on the wrong foot.</b> Barely more than twenty pages in I was </span>
  <span id="freeText15424190177935277438" style="display:none"><b>The magic is gone.</b><br /><br />This is not the sequel I had hoped for when I closed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18079804.Half_Bad__Half_Bad___1_" title="Half Bad (Half Bad, #1) by Sally Green" rel="nofollow noopener">Half Bad</a> last year, exhilarated and excited for the next installment. I'm going to be completely honest and say I found myself skim-reading parts of the second half because it just could not hold my attention. So if you do happen to read this and discover something amazing, it's possible that it happened while I was busy not caring.<br /><br />Okay. What went wrong?<br /><br /><b>We started off on the wrong foot.</b> Barely more than twenty pages in I was forced to do a double take when I read:<br /><br /><i>"Her skin is soft and skin-coloured."</i><br /><br />Bad use of descriptions aside, I cringed when I tried to conjure an image of what "skin-coloured" could possibly mean. Not surprisingly, the character in question - Annalise - is white. Fuck knows what colour skin other ethnicities supposedly have.<br /><br />The first few chapters are filled with Nathan's dreams of Annalise: touching her, exchanging bland conversation, staring at her skin-coloured skin and eye-coloured eyes (blue, I'd wager). It's like everything evil, nasty and fast-paced has just been sucked out of this story. I can sum up about 80% of the plot into nothing more than <b>finding and saving Annalise.</b> Oh shucks, somebody please save the blonde-haired, blue-eyed, white chick who's landed herself in some kind of magical coma. It's like Disney's Sleeping Beauty, with about the same amount of non-white people.<br /><br />But this is just an ARC and people make stupid mistakes, right? Surely the author didn't intend to make it sound like that, right? So I continued on. A couple of chapters later (Nathan wanders around thinking about his dad and - you guessed it - Annalise during this time), <b>the most Australian character I've ever encountered appears</b>. Nathan describes him as having an Australian accent, and yet this is not enough, because the author throws in a couple of "crikeys!" and "mate"s whenever he speaks, just so we fully appreciate his Australianness. <br /><br />Maybe you think I'm nitpicking. Maybe you think racist descriptions and cultural stereotypes are no big deal. I disagree, but whatever, it's not like I needed them for this book to be <b>so unbelievably boring.</b> I mean... what is the story here beyond Nathan's obsession with Annalise and her skin? Seriously. The book opens with him thinking about her and wanting to find her. 50% in and he still hasn't found her, but I honestly wish I'd counted how many times he thinks "I must find Annalise" or "I need to save Annalise" during that time. It felt like every single page.<br /><br />And Annalise is so annoying. She doesn't have much of a personality, she just slots into the story where she's needed, doing whatever the author needs her to do to move the story in a certain direction whilst being all blonde and pretty. <b>Like that stupid ending and what it seems to promise for the next book.</b> Without giving away any spoilers, the final few lines are:<br /><br /><i>...if it hadn't been for Annalise.<br />You lie in the rain. Going over it again and again. There's nothing else you can do today. But tomorrow will be different. Tomorrow you go after her.</i><br /><br />Oh my effin' god. <b>So the next book's going to be about finding Annalise as well?!</b> No, thank you. I've had enough Annalise for a lifetime.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://mycountryheart.co.uk/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15424190177935277438" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7305686813247925247"><b>SPOILER</b> only if you haven't read the first book :)<br/><br/>Who don't ship Nathan and Gabriel? <br/><br/>I've never read a novel where the hero ends up with the gay boy in stead of the too-perfect heroine.   <span id="freeText7305686813247925247" style="display:none"><b>SPOILER</b> only if you haven't read the first book :)<br /><br />Who don't ship Nathan and Gabriel? <br /><br />I've never read a novel where the hero ends up with the gay boy in stead of the too-perfect heroine. I hope this one makes the exception. <br /><br /><br /><b>My actual review</b><br /><br />I don't know how I feel about this book. I read it and I thought about the unfairness of this world. The white witches (the bad ones) remind me of sexist and racist people in real life and it made me feel depressed and mad. Out of topic and crazy I know. But that's what happened.<br /><br />The first quarter was slow but things got serious in the last quarter. So I guess it made up for Nathan's annoying whining about Annalise.<br /><br />One thing though. I don't get how Gabrielle is so in love with Nathan. It's understandable for Nathan to be infuriated like that with Annlise. She is like the only beautiful and pure thing in his dark and hellish life after all. He is bound to love her. But Gabriel, how can he love Nathan more than his life? *shrug* I guess he sees something in him. I don't know.<br /><br />Looking forward to the next book. :)</span>

<div id="review_895830095" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/895830095" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/895830095?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141350882" href="/book/show/22429853-half-wild">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=ya-male-narrators">ya-male-narrators</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=reread">reread</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer895830095" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9584023912929376704"><b>READ #2 Nov 2017</b>:<br/>You know how you go back to read a book and suddenly remember how much it meant to you?? <b>Hi. It's me right now.</b> I seriously can't sum up my love for this series. It's complex and brutal and so so messy and bloody and MY HEART. I think it fell on the floor?? I think I am a small black hole of destructive feelings but oh my god. I love this book.<br/><br/><b>Notable Things:</b><br/>• I loved it even better the second time<br/>• audiobook is still 5000% the most perfect thing<br/>• can British people pls read all</span>
  <span id="freeText9584023912929376704" style="display:none"><b>READ #2 Nov 2017</b>:<br />You know how you go back to read a book and suddenly remember how much it meant to you?? <b>Hi. It's me right now.</b> I seriously can't sum up my love for this series. It's complex and brutal and so so messy and bloody and MY HEART. I think it fell on the floor?? I think I am a small black hole of destructive feelings but oh my god. I love this book.<br /><br /><b>Notable Things:</b><br />• I loved it even better the second time<br />• audiobook is still 5000% the most perfect thing<br />• can British people pls read all audiobooks of ever, yes that would be nice<br />• Something I love so much is how the book not only deals with violence and abuse, but it discusses the after-affects and psychology of it. It makes it SO REAL.<br />• Nathan is actually my most favourite violent cinnamon child.<br />• I violently ship him and Gabriel<br />• if Annalise fell in a very deep pond I would be okay with that.<br />• SERIOUSLY SHE FREAKING ANNOYS ME SHE IS VERY SHALLOW.<br />• I remember being offended at how cliche Nesbitt's Australianness is last time? but wait wait wait...no. We are truly like that wow.<br />• I forgot how interesting Marcus is and I kind of love him and that's bad so yeah nevermind me<br />• This is so. freaking. bloody and I love my YA dark<br />• I am a bucket of feelings<br />• There is war and moral and ethical questions and there is blood and desperation and the craving of love. The way Nathan just craves love ajfdkslad.<br />• help<br />• I love this series so much<br /><br /><br /><b>READ #1: March 2015</b><br /><br /><b>OH WHERE DO EVEN BEGIN TO EXPLAIN MY FEELS-EXPLOSION?!!</b> I love this series. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18079804.Half_Bad__The_Half_Bad_Trilogy___1_" title="Half Bad (The Half Bad Trilogy, #1) by Sally Green" rel="nofollow noopener">Half Bad</a> was a completely surprise for me, because I just never expected to love it to such an astronomical amount. I CANNOT EVEN EXPLAIN MY LOVE FOR HALF BAD. The writing! The characters! The story! And did Half Wild disappoint? Um, heck no. <b>Half Wild was amazing and bloody and tearful and intense.</b> I need book 3 like I need air. I NEED IT. HOW AM I TO WAIT TO 2016 FOR IT?!!!<br /><br />Okay, okay.<br /><br />Where shall we begin?<br /><br />How about the writing...The style is gorgeous and unconventional and so, so absorbed in Nathan's mind. I mean, <i>obviously</i>...it's <i>by</i> Nathan after all, right? But it's his VOICE. It's so incredibly unique and always true to him. And sometimes Nathan loses it and we don't just see it in the actions, we see it in how the writing is on the page. Things get jerky. When he uses his Gift, the capitals drop off to represent his wild, animalistic state. And when he panics, we SEE it as well as read it. <br /><br />Nathan is totally wild and unhinged and scared and messed up. AND HE IS JUST SO INCREDIBLY WRITTEN THAT HE FEELS REAL. I just...wow. He's one of my top-favourite characters of the universe. <br /><br />And of course, there's so much <b>Gabriel</b> in this book. Gabriel is missing at the beginning, but it's hardly a spoiler to say he turns up because...um, DUH. Gabriel is as adorable as ever...<i>but</i> definitely more angsty and angry in this one. After all, he loves Nathan so much he'll follow Nathan to his grave. Even when Nathan continually friendzones Gabriel...and goes after Annalise. <br /><br />So let's talk about the triangle, okay?! <b>There definitely is a love-triangle, although it's a gorgeous one and hardly cliche.</b> It did bother me a little though, because Nathan is totally leading Gabriel on (hello, what about that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[kiss?!! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>) and yet he's in love with Annalise. It's unfair. I realise Nathan is messed up and has been tortured and abused ALL his life. He doesn't know what he wants. He's so confused and torn between Annalise and Gabriel (THOUGH THE SHIP IS KINDA CLEAR, NATHAN, YOU IDIOT. Do we say Gathan or Nabriel?). And I found the progression of the triangle pretty...predictable. Which is a little disappointing. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Particularly when I KNEW since Nathan was keeping Kieren's death (and you know, the fact that Nathan MURDERED Kieren pretty bloodily) a secret from Annalise was going to destroy their relationship. I KNEW IT. So I found it kind of a let down when it all played out 100% how I predicted. But the fact that it ends with Nathan deciding he's going to hunt/kill Annalise?! OH MY GOSH. HOLD MY FROZEN FEELS. I'M DYING HERE!!!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br /><b>It's still got a few funny moments.</b> I <i>adore</i> humour. And Nesbitt, the Australian half-black Witch, half-fain, was hilarious. Although when he appeared he was "Crickey mate" to everything which is...kind of offensive. Australians DON'T talk like that. HELLO I AM AUSTRALIAN. And Nesbitt pretty quickly dropped that way of speaking and, you know, acted normal. Um. Okay then. BUT PFFT. Nesbitt was still hilarious and I loved his and Nathan's relationship (which was so much "shut up or I'll stab your eyeball with a spork"...I know, I sound crazy, but it was funny IN CONTEXT). And Nathan also has a bit of dry wit coming in there. Like something will go drastically wrong and he views it in an almost sardonic way. I loved that!<br /><br /><b>BUT THE ENDONG OMG. THE ENDING.</b> It's not an awful cliffhanger, but the prelude?! HOLD MY BLEEDING HEART (um, literally, in the book) BUT I DIDN'T THINK IT WOULD END LIKE THIS. I wasn't dumb enough to hope for happiness (in this book?! HA HA HA. no.) but ohhhh, it was bloody and sad and someone INCREDIBLE dies and I was pretty much clutching the pages whispering, "No no no." I want book 3 ASAP. I want it yesterday. <br /><br /><b>I seriously cannot recommend this series enough.</b> The best part of it is it plays with "grey areas". White Witches aren't just good and Black Witches aren't just bad. (Actually EVERYONE is awful and cruel.) It's about morals and revenge and family. There's some sweet moments, but mostly there's tears and bloodshed. Witches aren't exactly original, but this series manages to spin them in SUCH a different way that I'm 100% glued to the page the ENTIRE TIME. Although if I did have to pick a favourite, I <i>would</i> say book 1: Half Bad, was better. The ending of Half Wild was incredible but a little too rushed and almost anti-climatic in some of the heart-rending death deliveries. BUT PFFT, I DON'T CARE. I'M A FAN.<br /><br />SOMEONE NEEDS TO PLUCK NATHAN FROM THIS BOOK AND GIVE HIM A NICE WARM HAPPY HOME. He is so so mistreated all of the time. And yet it doesn't make him a whingy poor hopeless character He's STILL fighting. Although he makes idiot mistakes and he's obviously deluded about Annalise, but pffft. We'll forgive him. He was probably dropped on his head as a baby, you know, poor darling little chap.<br /><br /><b>Basically I love this series.</b> It's not average and THAT'S what I like to read.<br /><br /><br /><blockquote> "Don't worry about me, kid. The second you start to turn, I'm getting my gun out and shooting you."<br />I stare at him but, before I can think of anything to say, he adds, "Don't look so alarmed, mate, my aim's spot on. I'd just wing you. You heal quick - no harm done."<br />And from his voice I know he's serious. I mumble to Gabriel, "See? People ask you to show your Gift by turning into Obama; me, they shoot and say 'No harm done.'"</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="9584023912929376704" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18974711-darth-j?shelf=witch-wizard">witch-wizard</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1249327916" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer6500771750007034137">1.5 Stars<br/><br/><b>A somewhat interesting plot with terrible writing, but mostly a chore to read. </b><br/><br/>The book starts off with this annoying formatting:<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429024334i/14517124._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>And then it continues at other points throughout the book too:<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429024334i/14517125._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>And it’s not just the formatting that’s bad. I’ve said <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1220222648?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>previously that parts of the first book felt too much like a rough draft</a> , the same is true here. While whole sections in this book read smoothly, others are too <b>unpolished and amateurish</b>. One of two things needs to happen for this series, eithe</span>
  <span id="freeText6500771750007034137" style="display:none">1.5 Stars<br><br><b>A somewhat interesting plot with terrible writing, but mostly a chore to read. </b><br><br>The book starts off with this annoying formatting:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429024334i/14517124._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>And then it continues at other points throughout the book too:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429024334i/14517125._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And it’s not just the formatting that’s bad. I’ve said <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1220222648?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">previously that parts of the first book felt too much like a rough draft</a> , the same is true here. While whole sections in this book read smoothly, others are too <b>unpolished and amateurish</b>. One of two things needs to happen for this series, either 1. Green needs to get a new editor or 2. Green needs to just plot out the book and get someone else to write it à la James Patterson. The author has the bones of a fascinating story but putting it onto paper is something that is clearly not in her skill set. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ And there are a few passages that are purposefully without capitals, but the audience is left to assume that is because the MC has transformed into a wolf?? and doesn’t have the brain power to use proper punctuation when in this form. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Further, this book is <b>mostly filler</b>. I’ve said the previous installment read like an overlong prologue, and this one seems like more of the same. It’s clear the author is setting up for a big finale but there needs to be more development and less running around in the woods. Here’s how this book read: We’re in the woods/I’m an animal and don’t understand things/Woods again/Major character death/Woods/Animal/Woods/Major character death/Woods/Animal/Oh hey, there’s the evil Marcus/Woods/Kill some hunters/Woods/Animal time/Woods/Major character death/Woods/Castle/Woods/”I love Annalise”/Woods/Animal/Woods/”Imma give Annalise some space”/Woods/Major character death/Woods/End<br><br>Did you notice that there were a lot of major character deaths? Well, they aren’t given any gravity and are quickly glossed over. Seriously, if you accidentally skip a sentence you missed a death scene. You can’t become invested in characters because they are all so flat and since the writing isn’t interested in making you feel anything, you simply don’t. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429024334i/14517126._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>What I did like was a new character named Van. She’s an expert with potions and seems the most developed of the new characters, which I take to mean that she is important and will die in the finale if I were to just follow the author’s previous pattern.<br><br>Sadly, I won’t ever get to know her fate because I will never read another book in this series. The first 2 were mostly <b>boring and felt like busy work</b>, and her writing style needs a vast improvement because her releases so far were <b>just not ready for bookstores</b>. Just as there are beautiful actresses that can't act, so too are there books that are <b>pretty but without any substance</b>; this was one of them. Even as a popcorn book, this was bland. I was fooled by the shiny covers and descriptions twice already, but I won’t be again.<br><br>In summation, <b>this is just as forgettable as the first one.</b><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_890869372" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/890869372" />
    <a title="O.R." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22294728-o-r"><img alt="O.R." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1440878296p2/22294728.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/890869372?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="O.R." class="user" itemprop="url" name="O.R." href="/user/show/22294728-o-r">O.R.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22294728-o-r?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22294728-o-r?shelf=beautiful">beautiful</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22294728-o-r?shelf=love">love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer890869372" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11400444225090358630">2.01.2016<br/>I will try to re-read first two books before the release of third and hopefully write a more coherent review ;)<br/><br/>OMG<br/>Officially best author ever. <br/>Now I am just really embarrassed for not keeping it eloquent, though *burns* . This is what happens when you write a review right after reading a book and don't expect anyone to read it. Especially authors. I'm sorry.<br/>But, oh my gosh, I'm so touched <3<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427749615i/14316913._SY540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/><br/>---<br/><br/>I feel weird after this ending O.O it was good, just... To be upset and really WOWed at the sa</span>
  <span id="freeText11400444225090358630" style="display:none">2.01.2016<br>I will try to re-read first two books before the release of third and hopefully write a more coherent review ;)<br><br>OMG<br>Officially best author ever. <br>Now I am just really embarrassed for not keeping it eloquent, though *burns* . This is what happens when you write a review right after reading a book and don't expect anyone to read it. Especially authors. I'm sorry.<br>But, oh my gosh, I'm so touched &lt;3<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427749615i/14316913._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br>---<br><br>I feel weird after this ending O.O it was good, just... To be upset and really WOWed at the same time uh... Weird feeling<br><br>26.03.15<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1427382521ra/14267245.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>SPOILERS<br><br>In the middle of the book I was ready to drop to 3 stars, but I guess it would be unfair considering I gave worse books 5 stars, and this book won me over at the end again. <br><br>I have a lot of thoughts.<br><br>So the first half, maybe a little over half of the book was amazing. When it comes to fantasy books, Half Bad trilogy is right after Harry Potter.<br>It is definitely one of my favourite trilogies. <br>There are many things that this series have that other YA is missing badly:<br>1. Character isn't a Mary Sue.<br>2. Character acts badass, not says s/he is badass and then everybody does everything for them.<br>3. Characters KILL. The protagonists KILLS. <br>4. And then do not weep over it. It had to be done and that's it. Yeah finally.<br>5. This is a story about the "bad" side with a twist.<br><br>Now, everything was going great. The story focused on Gabriel/Nathan and we were also introduced to new characters. They all grew on me. I loved the relationships. I loved each character separately.<br>There are women, there are men, and they're all different yet equally badass and interesting. They're mature characters. They're fun to read. No one annoys you. <br>Gabriel and Nathan's relationship is one of the most interesting I have read in a while and I "ship" them beyond anything. Their relationship develops beautifully and realistically. <br><br>Here is the thing - the problem was not triangle. It was simply Nathan/Anna on their own. <br>We spent over 200 pages reading the amazing relationship of Gabriel and Nathan. It isn't about Gabriel finding Nathan hot and wanting to hook up with him. They love being together. They like talking, exercising, they understand each other, trust each other, they miss each other, Nathan falls and falls deeper into love [which he denies hard, but in my opinion it is obvious]. You can see how nicely his feelings develop. They just work together.<br>And then Anna makes a come back.<br>It isn't the triangle - it is not Nathan whining he does not know who to choose, playing with two people at once, who are unaware. No. <br>Gabriel is aware of Nathan's feelings for Annalise and made his choice to go after him anyway. Anna is later made aware of Gabriel's feelings. Nathan informed both, told Gabriel than Anna is his love, told Anna that Gabriel is just his friend. So it's not a problem. The worst thing about triangles isn't there.<br>I'd feel awfully bad for Gabriel, but he could make his choice, he wasn't played with, and I'd accept Anna/Nathan if this was Nathan's fair choice. You do not choose who you fall in love with.<br>It also helps that Gabriel knows when to say what he thinks, and he does not hide anything. He calls Nathan out on his shit. Bless.<br><br>The problem is that Nathan/Anna is cringe worthy. Triangle or not. <br><br>There are, in my opinion, two reasons;<br>1. After you develop one relationship for over 200 pages, and you do it well, the readers will get attached. So when after 200 pages you suddenly bring that other person back, and throw her into a bed with him, no one will feel it. I hated reading those scenes. I do not understand why Anna/Nathan like each other. They don't even know each other. It was only about, sorry for the harsh word, screwing each other. There was no development, absolutely nothing made me feel wow they fit.<br>All the time to develop a relationship was given to Nathan/Gabriel. I understand why they should be together. I get it. I see it. Them ending up together would make sense and I'd be happy.<br>Anna/Nathan... no.<br>2. Anna is the worst character. Naive princess living in a fairytale, like everything that happened did not happen to her. WAKE UP, GIRL. The whole cast is full of really interesting, badass guys and women. Anna is a 12 year old who does nothing but giggles, makes out with Nathan, and calls him a prince. I don't know who cringed more, me or Gabriel. In such a great setting, war, blood, murders... suddenly giggling "I love yous" more giggling and sex. There was nothing behind this. It made me nearly skip the pages, I begged this girl to go back to that deadly sleep. It was so... out of place. Especially since they could not even stop themselves in front of Gabriel. And that's nasty. <br>Since the beginning there wasn't much to this relationship, but liking each other's looks. Wanting to make out. Being very childish. Nathan suddenly naive and putting others in danger for her, even though she never prioritised his safety over others and he was hurt because of her. <br>No. Just no. <br><br>But here is the thing - a very personal thought. I think that Sally wants Nathan/Gabriel to end up together. I think this is why Nathan/Anna was so bad, especially since I read the ending that flashed a new light on the story. IF I did not read that interview and get impression from the book, I am not sure if I would read the third book. Couldn't we have a few less descriptions at least? Heh. It is just me, though, you know I take books personally and get too attached, so relationships can win or lose me. <br>Sally said that she, at the beginning, had N/G together in the first book already but then decided to split their relationship for three books so it won't be boring and well, development. And, well, the development is beautiful. Them ending up together at the end will result in a fantastic relationship. Let's be honest, believable relationships aren't a thing in YA. This might be first. Typical shallow relationship is Anna/Nathan - without depth, just making out, giggling [Im sorry but it annoyed me so much, omg] and nothing else.<br>BUT<br>SPOILER SPOILER SPOILER<br>It actually was proven it does not work. Like Gabriel said, in other words, that relationship is too shallow to work. And at the end it was proven.<br>Hard. I can't believe she did that. Knowing what they did to Nathan she still prioritised her assholish brothers over him and did THAT. Knowing how much he meant to Nathan. Sick. Once again she prioritised them over him and that in such cruel way. In my opinion it clearly showed she does not care for him. This is not love. <br>(He better not forgive her. And if they will then consider even a friendship... No. Enough.) everybody warned him and the worst happened because of his naivety. <br>In a way now I don't hate this relationship so much because it definitely brought a heartbreaking but very interesting plot. I just wish there was less description when they were still together, you know. <br>If this is all going where I think it does - one word: badass. This will be war, and I can't wait for it. I don't have a problem with crappy relationships if there is a point to them, instead of them being treated like they're perfect. <br>I love that characters own their pluses and minuses in this series.<br><br>God that ending made me hate her. I liked HIM. I swore at her. At least Nathan had a correct response. He better keep it. I want to see that! That's the thing, at least Sally's characters always have correct responses. There is no bullshit. I hope Nathan's way of thinking won't change. It shouldn't be only him wanting to get revenge either, so it should be interesting. Gabriel will need to bite his tongue to not say "told you". Nathan deserves to hear it, to be fair.<br><br>I found this a faster read than the first and more enjoyable. Well, Nathan was free, so the book was not as difficult. I had to take breaks from Half Bad because it just hurt to read sometimes. It's not a bad thing, but I enjoyed less pain here, heh. And Nathan/Gabriel made me read very quickly. <br>- Nathan/Gabriel scenes - So much love. <br>- So much yes for characters who DO not just TALK. No whining, no others doing for them yet them getting worshipped, etc etc. You know. <br>- Everybody loves Gabriel and finds him hot, I love it. He gets love whether Nathan is there or not. He wasn't created just to be there for Nathan and that's amazing. <br><br>So, yeah, just skip through Nathan/Anna scenes and this is definitely one of my favourite 2015 reads. <br>----<br><br><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426187524i/13985885.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>I CANT WAIT ANY LONGER <br>[12.02.15]<br><br>I can't wait.<br>I need to find out what's going to happen to Nathan, to Gabriel, and to them as a relationship. <br><br>LOOK AT THE PERFECT COVER REVEALED TODAY 7.07.2014<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1404753258i/10278374._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Nathan/Gabriel relationship:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1404756356i/10278725.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>updated 8.08.14<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1407535348i/10735902.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1407012016i/10627183.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_1225601590" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1225601590" />
    <a title="Mai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12295071-mai"><img alt="Mai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1477760638p2/12295071.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1225601590?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mai" href="/user/show/12295071-mai">Mai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141350882" href="/book/show/22429853-half-wild">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12295071-mai?shelf=books-in-my-room">books-in-my-room</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12295071-mai?shelf=underrated">underrated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12295071-mai?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1225601590" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15887192920868833425">I should probably go and wash my face. I've been crying like a baby for the last five minutes now. I'll stop crying and get back to writing this review.<br/><br/>Okay, so <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20814989.Half_Wild__The_Half_Bad_Trilogy___2_' title='Half Wild (The Half Bad Trilogy, #2) by Sally Green' rel='nofollow noopener'> Half Wild</a> picks up where <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18079804.Half_Bad__The_Half_Bad_Trilogy___1_' title='Half Bad (The Half Bad Trilogy, #1) by Sally Green' rel='nofollow noopener'> Half Bad</a> ended, it continues on with Nathan's life as a Half Code who is hated by pure white witches and wanted dead for being the son of the most dangerous black witch, Marcus Edge.<br/><br/>I was very scared I'll end up hating this book because it seems like sequels are always worse than the first book. However, I prob</span>
  <span id="freeText15887192920868833425" style="display:none">I should probably go and wash my face. I've been crying like a baby for the last five minutes now. I'll stop crying and get back to writing this review.<br /><br />Okay, so <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20814989.Half_Wild__The_Half_Bad_Trilogy___2_" title="Half Wild (The Half Bad Trilogy, #2) by Sally Green" rel="nofollow noopener"> Half Wild</a> picks up where <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18079804.Half_Bad__The_Half_Bad_Trilogy___1_" title="Half Bad (The Half Bad Trilogy, #1) by Sally Green" rel="nofollow noopener"> Half Bad</a> ended, it continues on with Nathan's life as a Half Code who is hated by pure white witches and wanted dead for being the son of the most dangerous black witch, Marcus Edge.<br /><br />I was very scared I'll end up hating this book because it seems like sequels are always worse than the first book. However, I probably have hatred running through my veins at this point, I'm a mixture of feelings and the dominate one is totally <s>pain</s> anger.<br /><br />This book was magnificent, interesting and intense. It was absolutely magical. Every part of it was intense, I felt closer to the characters, and got hurt when they did. The writing style was amazing, I couldn't put the book down or pass a chapter without commenting <s>- poor goodreads -</s> on it, I was completely absorbed into the story that I tuned everything else out.<br /><br />The characters' development was one of the best things about this book. And the addition of new characters was what made this book even more exciting.<br />I don't know how but Sally Green managed to make <i>Gabriel</i> even more appealing, how can a character be so perfect and so good at continuing to be even more perfect? I don't know, but I've never read about someone that soft and gentle and beautiful! The relationship between him and Nathan grows and develops into something intense and unfair, Nathan can be quite selfish when he wants to be and Gabriel is being the lovely petal that he is and goes all <b>you-kiss-me-I-kiss-you-you-scratch-my-back-I-scratch-yours</b> on Nathan, but guess what Nathan does? uh-huh.<br /><br />The lost star goes for Annalise, this book was all about Annalise -who is the reason why I have cried my eyes out- and how she is just a piece of useless Gretchen Weiners, I usually like girlfriends but this one was dumb and good for nothing, she was just a magnet for bad luck and brought crap upon others.<br />Also loads of events happened fast at the end while I wanted it to be more detailed and slow burned, and some characters were unfairly treated, I felt bad for some.<br /><br />All in all, I'm in love with this trilogy so far, it's completely meeting my expectations even surprising me with how marvelous it is, incredible writing and fantastic plot!</span>

          </span>

    <a title="majo " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39317215-majo"><img alt="majo " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577812855p2/39317215.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1746045661?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="majo " class="user" itemprop="url" name="majo " href="/user/show/39317215-majo">majo </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39317215-majo?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39317215-majo?shelf=year-2018">year-2018</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39317215-majo?shelf=fav-protagonist">fav-protagonist</a>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1746045661" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8762120730406213768">THIS BOOK WAS EVERYTHING I WANTED AND MORE<br/><br/><b>I loved the brutality of it</b>. <br/><br/>I loved the tough decisions the protagonist has to make, and that he's not afraid to make them.<br/><br/>I loved that the main character, Nathan understands that in times of war you have to kill, you have to be cruel, vicious, bad. Because in war it is you and the ones you love or the others, and <b>a lot of times in YA books, protagonists don't understand the importance and the necessity of being selfish and harsh and cruel and bloody.</b> T</span>
  <span id="freeText8762120730406213768" style="display:none">THIS BOOK WAS EVERYTHING I WANTED AND MORE<br /><br /><b>I loved the brutality of it</b>. <br /><br />I loved the tough decisions the protagonist has to make, and that he's not afraid to make them.<br /><br />I loved that the main character, Nathan understands that in times of war you have to kill, you have to be cruel, vicious, bad. Because in war it is you and the ones you love or the others, and <b>a lot of times in YA books, protagonists don't understand the importance and the necessity of being selfish and harsh and cruel and bloody.</b> There is no other option. It is a war, after all. But Nathan, my precious murderous baby, understand this and I love him for it.<br /><br />I loved Nathan discovering his gift and learning to control it.<br /><br />And I love Gabriel. He's the kind of guy Nathan deserves and now, more than ever, I need them to be together.<br /><br />And specially I loved the ending of this book. It is the kind of ending that leaves you wanting more. This trilogy has been absolutely fascinating to me. <br /><br />Oh! btw, <u>I have never hated a character more than I hate Annalise now.</u> (fucking bitch).</span>
  <a data-text-id="8762120730406213768" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1218368531" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1218368531" />
    <a title="Claire (Book Blog Bird)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10982678-claire-book-blog-bird"><img alt="Claire (Book Blog Bird)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1343948552p2/10982678.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1218368531?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Claire (Book Blog Bird)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Claire (Book Blog Bird)" href="/user/show/10982678-claire-book-blog-bird">Claire (Book Blog Bird)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10982678-claire-book-blog-bird?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1218368531" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7212278550293805930">I received a copy of Half Wild in exchange for an honest review, courtesy of Penguin Random House UK and Netgalley. A copy of this review is also on my blog: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.bookblogbird.weebly.com'>www.bookblogbird.weebly.com</a><br/><br/>I finished the first book in this trilogy a couple of days ago. It’s a wild, gruesome ride and I loved every minute of it.<br/><br/>This book, not so much.<br/><br/>I want to start by highlighting the good parts. Some scenes were great. There are a couple of scenes with Gabriel and Nathan that almost had me in tears, they were so bea</span>
  <span id="freeText7212278550293805930" style="display:none">I received a copy of Half Wild in exchange for an honest review, courtesy of Penguin Random House UK and Netgalley. A copy of this review is also on my blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bookblogbird.weebly.com">www.bookblogbird.weebly.com</a><br /><br />I finished the first book in this trilogy a couple of days ago. It’s a wild, gruesome ride and I loved every minute of it.<br /><br />This book, not so much.<br /><br />I want to start by highlighting the good parts. Some scenes were great. There are a couple of scenes with Gabriel and Nathan that almost had me in tears, they were so beautifully written. The parts with Marcus in were very good, too.<br /><br />Also, I genuinely think Sally Green is a great writer. With a trilogy about witches, magic and superpowers, it would have been easy to have gone completely purple-prose and hammed it up. She does none of that. Her writing is very gritty and very real.<br /><br />There were some characters that I loved. Nathan is one of the most interesting protagonists I’ve read about for a long time and it was fascinating to watch him embrace his Black Witch side. Marcus, his father, I found very compelling also and I think it takes a very skilled writer to make a mass murderer a sympathetic character. And Gabriel. Aaah...Gabriel. Fit, gorgeous, witty, able to handle a gun and utterly devoted to Nathan. <br /><br />Unfortunately, I had a bit of a problem with some of the other characters. Annalise was one, and a lot of the plot revolved around her. I thought she was a complete drip and I couldn’t for the life of me see why Nathan was so obsessed with her. She had no spark. She wasn’t witty, she wasn’t useful in a fight, she didn’t really know whether she wanted to join the Alliance, she didn’t even know what her Gift was, for crying out loud. She was just a pretty face. Blah.<br /><br />I get that seventeen year old boys often think with their junk instead of their heads when it comes to girls, but Nathan is such a complex character that I felt his obsession with this one-dimensional Disney-Princess girl was wrong. Just...wrong.<br /><br />Also, it didn’t help the Annalise-Is-Great cause when she explained that the reason she left Nathan to be carved to bits by her psychotic brother (back in Half Bad) was because her parents locked her in her room. Huh? That’s not good. You shimmy out the window, or you break the lock, or you punch your dad in the face. You don’t just sit there and wait for the boy you love to be butchered.<br /><br />I had problems with the plot as well and the biggest problem was that there just didn’t seem to be one. The first half of the book revolves around finding Annalise. Nathan, Gabriel and two new characters (whose names I’ve already forgotten) just seem to zoom about all over Europe, without anything much actually happening. There are a couple of good bits, but they are few and far between and after the all-thriller-no-filler excitement of Half Bad it just fell a little flat. It felt like the author put all of her awesomest ideas into Half Bad, but couldn’t quite seem to think of anything to happen in this book.<br /><br />I know Sophomore Slump is a thing, where the eager-beaver author proudly delivers the final, final draft of the first instalment of their trilogy and the publisher goes, ‘Thanks very much. You now have exactly-’ Looks at watch ‘-three months to produce the first draft of the next instalment. GO! GO! GO!’<br /><br />Let me reiterate: I enjoy Sally Green’s writing and I would happily read a different series of hers, if she writes one, or a standalone and I kind of want to know what happens to Nathan and Gabriel, but I just don’t think I have the energy to read the third instalment.<br /><br />4/10</span>
  <a data-text-id="7212278550293805930" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6426259801582513491" style="display:none">3.5ish stars maybe... I really loved book one and its darkness, from the uncomfortable confusion of the beginning to the fear and adrenaline later on. I know it was a Marmite book, but I really loved it! This one just didn't have the substance. <br /><br />Don't get me wrong, I enjoyed Half Wild. I liked the 'animal' development and the shift in relationships with Gabrielle, Annalise and Marcus. It all makes sense and probably needed to happen. It's just that on the whole it felt a little 'filler'. Compared to book 1 this was slow, and not a great deal happened. Plenty of deaths and gore, which is definitely a redeeming feature, but for a story now turning towards all-out war it was a bit lacking in action until the last few chapters. But then it definitely delivered, and I'm left hanging waiting for book 3, with some vengeance I can't wait to see!</span>

<div id="review_938367236" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/938367236" />
    <a title="Luis Moller" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28579519-luis-moller"><img alt="Luis Moller" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1392086895p2/28579519.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/938367236?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Luis Moller" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Luis Moller" href="/user/show/28579519-luis-moller">Luis Moller</a>
      </span>

          marked it as to-read




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer938367236" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2356202163577420414">I'm all for a gay protagonist as it is missing from mainstream YA literature but I don't think having Gabriel and Nathan end up together would be the greatest of choices. My reasoning is this: We are told the story in Nathan's perspective but we are never told of any occurrences were he has had either homosexual thoughts or urges. We meet Gabriel who is gay and yet we still do not get any information if Nathan might actually lean that way. We just know that he has been in love with Annalise sinc</span>
  <span id="freeText2356202163577420414" style="display:none">I'm all for a gay protagonist as it is missing from mainstream YA literature but I don't think having Gabriel and Nathan end up together would be the greatest of choices. My reasoning is this: We are told the story in Nathan's perspective but we are never told of any occurrences were he has had either homosexual thoughts or urges. We meet Gabriel who is gay and yet we still do not get any information if Nathan might actually lean that way. We just know that he has been in love with Annalise since like forever, what does this lead a reader to believe? Nathan has never really had any homosexual thoughts or urges for him to even be curious of his sexuality. I am sorry but no one can just wake up one morning and say "OMG I am gay" without any past history of homosexuality. You are born straight, gay, lesbian, bisexual, or transsexual. You can't choose what you are born. If Sally Green were to end up turning Nathan gay it would send a wrong message to the LGBT community. It would also kind of be a bad choice in terms of actual literary content as well. You can't write a debut novel of a series and introduce and develop a main character and then in the second novel add a completely and life changing revelation as homosexuality without at all hinting to it in the first book. I think that a homosexual protagonist would be given more justice in another novel. PLEASE DO NOT TAKE MY COMMENT AS HOMOPHOBIC CUZ I TOTALLY DO NOT MEAN IT TO BE.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2356202163577420414" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I'll just have to hope that in the last installment Sally will take a little more time to fill in the blanks (espec</span>
  <span id="freeText6187602310740399812" style="display:none">While superior to the first installment in characterization, plot, and writing, I am a little ticked off that the world building was not detailed any further. The reason why I never complained about the vague world-building in the first book was because I thought that was all the information given to Nathan about it, and I was lead to believe it would grow as the series progressed. I'll just have to hope that in the last installment Sally will take a little more time to fill in the blanks (especially the question on whether or not "normal" people know about witches because I'm still pretty confused).<br><br>Review to come. <br><br><br><b>EDIT (11.07.14):</b><br><blockquote>

Not only am I eager to see what happens next, I’m also thrilled to find that they’ve continued with Half Bad’s cover-theme. I absolutely adore the cover for Half Bad – it was eye catching and unique and so clever. It was what pulled me into Green’s work in the first place. And I’m so happy that they’ve continued the originality into the sequel and did not replace it with a photoshopped cover of some hot guy and some smoke. <br><br><br>... But dammit please tell me my ship with Nathan and Gabriel will actually set sail. I loath Annalise with a burning passion. Just -- just go away. Shoo.</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30983445-anna-enchanted-by-ya?shelf=twists-and-turns">twists-and-turns</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30983445-anna-enchanted-by-ya?shelf=coverly-love">coverly-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30983445-anna-enchanted-by-ya?shelf=action-packed">action-packed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30983445-anna-enchanted-by-ya?shelf=ultimate-cliffhanger">ultimate-cliffhanger</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30983445-anna-enchanted-by-ya?shelf=impossible-not-to-love">impossible-not-to-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30983445-anna-enchanted-by-ya?shelf=male-protagonist">male-protagonist</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1033459739" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1174452018227391864">Phenomenal. I understand how this series isn’t for everyone which is the case for <i>all</i> books, but it’s safe to say that I loved it! Half Bad always stuck in my mind because it was original with a creative writing style that I hadn’t experienced before, and its sequel was no different – plus more.<br/><br/>Action was present from the start along with the development of some truly fascinating relationships. Nathan is a brilliant main character because he’s not “purely good”; yes he kills, and yes he’s not al</span>
  <span id="freeText1174452018227391864" style="display:none">Phenomenal. I understand how this series isn’t for everyone which is the case for <i>all</i> books, but it’s safe to say that I loved it! Half Bad always stuck in my mind because it was original with a creative writing style that I hadn’t experienced before, and its sequel was no different – plus more.<br><br>Action was present from the start along with the development of some truly fascinating relationships. Nathan is a brilliant main character because he’s not “purely good”; yes he kills, and yes he’s not always remorseful about it though the decisions are not at all easy. Being inside his head could be chilling at times but meant also meant there was never a dull moment! The way his mindset changed at the very end blew me away, and I was So. Damn. Glad. Finally one of his so called “friends” who I’ve never liked will *fingers crossed* get their just desserts.<br><br>Helping him along the way is Gabriel: easily my favourite character. The way he stands by Nathan through thick and thin (even when he’s undeserving) just warmed my heart and makes me want to give him a hug! Such a beautiful, kind, caring soul I’m anxious to see where his story goes. Just a warning – if it doesn’t end with him and Nathan walking happily towards the sunset in their happily ever after… <i>I won’t be held responsible for my actions.</i><br><br>Which brings me to Annalise, who I don’t even want to talk about. Let’s just say I don’t like her. At all. And wish she died instead of going into the magic coma. But moving on… We are introduced to new characters who are weaved perfectly into the fast-pace story and make it that much more enjoyable.<br><br>The ending stole the show and means I simply cannot stop thinking about Half Wild. From going to a possible 4 star rating to 5 (I’d give it more if I could without a doubt) it has set the scene perfectly for Half Lost coming out, <i>oh damn</i>, March next year! Right now that feels like forever away, but it certainly gives me time to re-read the books as I can guarantee I’ll be doing sometime in the future.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429043723ra/14521255.gif" width="400" height="100" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Posted on: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://enchantedbyya.blogspot.co.uk/">http://enchantedbyya.blogspot.co.uk/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1174452018227391864" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_902699573" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/902699573" />
    <a title="Jessica (The Psychotic Nerd)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd"><img alt="Jessica (The Psychotic Nerd)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1382576238p2/8096484.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/902699573?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica (The Psychotic Nerd)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica (The Psychotic Nerd)" href="/user/show/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd">Jessica (The Psychotic Nerd)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=trilogies">trilogies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=hall-of-awesome-4-stars-or-more">hall-of-awesome-4-stars-or-more</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=series-books">series-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=waiting-on-wed">waiting-on-wed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=book-series-that-are-over-with">book-series-that-are-over-with</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=penguin-random-house">penguin-random-house</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=pov-dude">pov-dude</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer902699573" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18353795970196573172">This and other reviews can be found on <a href='http://thepsychoticnerd.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Psychotic Nerd</a><br/><br/><b>
  <u>MY THOUGHTS</u>
</b><br/>I enjoyed the first book in this series, so I was excited to finally dive into this sequel! This book does have middle book syndrome, so it's very slow-paced, but I still enjoyed it!<br/><br/>This book takes place shortly after the events of Half Bad. Gabriel is currently missing, or dead, and Nathan keeps checking to see if Gabriel has showed up. He also still has to evade the Hunters and to make things even more difficult, he's havi</span>
  <span id="freeText18353795970196573172" style="display:none">This and other reviews can be found on <a href="http://thepsychoticnerd.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Psychotic Nerd</a><br /><br /><b>
  <u>MY THOUGHTS</u>
</b><br />I enjoyed the first book in this series, so I was excited to finally dive into this sequel! This book does have middle book syndrome, so it's very slow-paced, but I still enjoyed it!<br /><br />This book takes place shortly after the events of Half Bad. Gabriel is currently missing, or dead, and Nathan keeps checking to see if Gabriel has showed up. He also still has to evade the Hunters and to make things even more difficult, he's having trouble controlling his Gift. Oh, let's not forget that he still needs to save Annalise. To top it all off, people now what him to join some kind of Alliance. The leader of the White Witches in Britain have no started to kill all Black Witches in Europe, as well as White Witches that don't 'agree'. The Alliance want to put a stop with it and think Nathan would be a great fighter for the cause. <br /><br />This book is really really slow-paced. Enough happened to keep me interested, but this book was mostly leading up to the next book. There's a whole lot of planning, deciding, flashbacks, and fighting. Some of it was important, but there weren't really huge action-packed events until the end.<br /><br />The writing and the world-building in this book is great! I know some people don't really like the oddness of some of the writing, but I think it's very interesting and unique! As for the world, I love it! It's a very harsh magic system, but I think it's very different and, again, I think it's very interesting! We don't get to learn a whole lot more about it, though, in this book, but the system is still there. In fact, it's becoming even more darker.<br /><br />As for romance, it's probably one of the oddest romance I've ever had in a book, and I've read hundreds. Gabriel likes Nathan and Nathan likes Annalise. Nathan thinks he only likes Gabriel as a friend. I say thinks because I really like Gabriel and I completely ship them. Annalise is okay, but she's kind of the typical girl character I see in YA. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>IN CONCLUSION</u>
</b><br />All in all, this book has middle book syndrome, so it is a bit slow, but it's still necessary. I love the imagination in this series and this book ended in such a climatic way, that I can't wait to read the next book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="18353795970196573172" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=arc-physical">arc-physical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=from-publishers">from-publishers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=age-young-adult">age-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=genre-fantasy">genre-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=genre-romance-slow-burn">genre-romance-slow-burn</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=diverse-characters">diverse-characters</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=genre-paranormal">genre-paranormal</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1144557606" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13721973646750086182">Nathan is back and with it comes his new found abilities. He's still on the run from the terror of the White Witches, but he's not alone. With a new round of characters and enemies he might know, Nathan finds out exactly what he's capable of. Being out in the wild suits him.<br/><br/>Half Bad had some pacing issues but there was no problem with this one because I was constantly engaged. Namely because there's a certain love interest that I want him to get with. I felt like Nathan could fare better with th</span>
  <span id="freeText13721973646750086182" style="display:none">Nathan is back and with it comes his new found abilities. He's still on the run from the terror of the White Witches, but he's not alone. With a new round of characters and enemies he might know, Nathan finds out exactly what he's capable of. Being out in the wild suits him.<br /><br />Half Bad had some pacing issues but there was no problem with this one because I was constantly engaged. Namely because there's a certain love interest that I want him to get with. I felt like Nathan could fare better with this person and I just liked this person so much more for him. This person is good for him in more ways than one. Loyal, kind, and so in love with Nathan that I'm pretty sure Nathan himself didn't want to admit it to himself. The other love interest fell apart for me, and I wholly didn't trust them. You can tell how I'm writing these people so vaguely because I don't want there to be any spoilers.<br /><br />There's the sudden urgency to get around the White Witches even more and this time Nathan indeed gets help. From people he may not expect either. I thought it was wonderfully paced and that ending! Geez..If I knew it would be such a climatic ending I would have waited until the last book. I found it interesting that his magical power manifests here even though I still don't know what kind it is exactly. I liked the world a whole lot more and even though there are parts where it's dragged on, I couldn't help but love the ending. It just brought it up one star for me.<br /><br />RATING 3/5<br /><br />QUOTES<br /><br />"If I can't control it I could kill anyone."<br /><br />"There's no right or wrong here."<br /><br />"I never had you down as a coward—so that shows how much I know about people."<br /><br />"I treasure every second with you. Every second. More than you know."<br /><br />"The point of being good is doing it when it's tough, not when it's easy."</span>
