<div id="review_1168659793" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1168659793" />
    <a title="Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3399699-rose"><img alt="Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386022874p2/3399699.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1168659793?book_show_action=true">Jan 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rose" href="/user/show/3399699-rose">Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=pretty-cover">pretty-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=glbt">glbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=ya-a-z-reading-challenge-2015">ya-a-z-reading-challenge-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=great-premise-lacking-execution">great-premise-lacking-execution</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=magic">magic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1168659793" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16605317526443369966"><b>Initial reaction:</b> Seriously, I want to love this series. I want to love it. There are parts of it that I want to applaud and sing praises for Sally Green at least in the idea of where she wants to take this series, but honestly - the execution leaves much to be desired. Much of this book I felt like I was waiting on my hands for something to happen, and when finally something significant and engaging does happen, it's near the end of the book.<br/><br/>I'll finish out this series, certainly, but I hope th</span>
  <span id="freeText16605317526443369966" style="display:none"><b>Initial reaction:</b> Seriously, I want to love this series. I want to love it. There are parts of it that I want to applaud and sing praises for Sally Green at least in the idea of where she wants to take this series, but honestly - the execution leaves much to be desired. Much of this book I felt like I was waiting on my hands for something to happen, and when finally something significant and engaging does happen, it's near the end of the book.<br /><br />I'll finish out this series, certainly, but I hope the last book isn't this plodding for details and development. Not holding my breath on that though, since this pretty much had the same problems as the previous book, with a few new ones to match.<br /><br /><b>Full review:</b><br /><br />Okay guys, soapbox coming. I wasn't really a fan of Sally Green's "Half Bad" and I was on the fence for following the trilogy into its second book, "Half Wild." Yet, my curiosity always gets the best of me, and I did admit that there were some moments of "Half Bad" that I actually liked. It was just that it wasn't developed enough for the world and realm and I felt a disconnect with the overarching narrative and MC (Nathan).<br /><br />This book pretty much features the same problems as the last one in my eyes, verbatim. Seriously there was really no improvement from the last book into this one for content with respect to narrative pacing or establishing a greater connection with Nathan as a protagonist. *sighs* And that frustrated me greatly. Nathan is still just at arms length for most of the narrative and for all the things that have happened to him, I can't seem to sympathize with his plight.<br /><br />In this book, it's a little clearer why because for a great measure of the book, nothing seems to happen. Nathan makes plans of what he wants to do, but doesn't act on them, and has all encompassing thoughts of Annalise as he tries to figure out a way to save her and get out of the bargain he made - to kill his father Marcus. The book does showcase Nathan struggling with the power inside of him - a beast who seems to relentlessly kill, but it's hard to get the urgency of that situation half the time because of the way Green chooses to narrate it - either in flashbacks or at a distance where it's not immediate or jarring enough to thrill the reader (at least *this* reader, anyway). Character deaths in the beginning and middle of this novel seem to happen quick and without much resonation or consequence, and that also frustrated me. I wanted to feel the tension and consequences of those scenes, dangnabit. Why would you want to skip over that or otherwise lack the intimacy needed for those scenes to hit home?<br /><br />This was yet another case in which the secondary cast was better than the purported leads (Nathan and Annalise). I loved Gabriel's character - I almost wish that he'd be the leading character of this series than Nathan because he had so many dimensions to feel for, between his grief over nearly losing Nathan and his affections, as well as his overarching role in the conflict and the losses he's suffered; I just connected with him better. Plus, I want to ship him and Nathan. I really do. Even more rare in consideration, I don't see many GLBT relationships in a magic dystopian thriller like this one and I want to say "PLEASE MAKE IT HAPPEN!!!" I just wish Nathan had more development behind him than what it's currently showing and the way it chooses to show his plight.<br /><br />Nesbitt was an okay character and interesting enough for comic relief in places, while being a flawed character in and of himself for his role in the narrative. I don't know if I liked the fact he was crafted with so many Aussie personality cliches, but I did appreciate his role in the story.<br /><br />I was glad to see that Marcus, Nathan's father, had a little more role and connectivity in this part of the story. I just wish it hadn't taken much of the dragging heels of the novel to reach that point closer to its end. <br /><br />I really don't care what happens to Annalise at this point. I was only lukewarm about her character in the first book, but I ended up not caring one way or another about her by the end of this book. She's just...not a well-crafted character at all. No dimensions, just a useless character, and I hate saying that about a MC female who should mean more in the overarching conflict of the novel. What's the point of her being there other than just being a love interest for Nathan? Really, I don't understand. She serves no purpose wand it's a further source of frustration to see what happens with her character as the novel approached its conclusion.<br /><br />Which brings me to the ending. Dude...if the rest of the book had managed to work that kind of tension better and throughout the novel in its entirety, maybe I'd have a much higher rating to give. But since it's so quick and sloppy with its handling, I can't give "Half Wild" that much credit. There were a few brutally violent scenes in the book, but much of them seemed more like background noise apart from the ending, which had a really heavy cost to Nathan in terms of his personal relationships and his role in the overarching conflict. Seems like Nathan's going to have a quest of vengeance and role to serve, but I hope that actually comes to fruition instead of just leading into a cop-out conclusion. I do plan on following this series to the end, but given the quality of this one, I'm not super excited about it because this book could've been much better in quality. MUCH better. And it didn't deliver, to be blunt about it.<br /><br />Overall score: 2.5/5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16605317526443369966" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1225268076" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1225268076" />
    <a title="Sonja ✧･ﾟ｡★*☾" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35853271-sonja"><img alt="Sonja ✧･ﾟ｡★*☾" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484219542p2/35853271.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1225268076?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sonja ✧･ﾟ｡★*☾" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sonja ✧･ﾟ｡★*☾" href="/user/show/35853271-sonja">Sonja ✧･ﾟ｡★*☾</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780141360140" href="/book/show/24577299-half-wild">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35853271-sonja?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35853271-sonja?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35853271-sonja?shelf=advance-reader-copy">advance-reader-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35853271-sonja?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1225268076" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17822681408109511091"><b>8.25/10</b><br/><blockquote>
  <b> I'm . . . it's like there's someone, some<i>thing</i> else living in me. And he comes out and takes over. But I know he's still me, another part of me, a completely wild, uncaring me.</b>
</blockquote><br/><b>'Half Wild' is truly better than 'Half Bad'</b> in my opinion. There's more world building and amazing character development. Marcus felt more life-like than in the first novel. In the first novel he read like a paper cut-out. Now he read like the MC's father and a somewhat evil person. <br/><br/>I also liked the way Nathan </span>
  <span id="freeText17822681408109511091" style="display:none"><b>8.25/10</b><br><blockquote>
  <b> I'm . . . it's like there's someone, some<i>thing</i> else living in me. And he comes out and takes over. But I know he's still me, another part of me, a completely wild, uncaring me.</b>
</blockquote><br><b>'Half Wild' is truly better than 'Half Bad'</b> in my opinion. There's more world building and amazing character development. Marcus felt more life-like than in the first novel. In the first novel he read like a paper cut-out. Now he read like the MC's father and a somewhat evil person. <br><br>I also liked the way Nathan developed as a character. He gets to know himself and his Gift. And he really grows as a character.<br><br>I definitely disliked Annalise - the MC's love interest - more in this novel. Nathan was just so obsessed and thinking so much about her till the point that it got quite annoying. Also, Annalise does something unforgivable near the end of the novel. So, <i>yeah</i>. I think she's an idiot.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1426323710ra/14002467.gif" width="250" height="175" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I LOVE GABRIEL. He's an amazing character. And he deserves the world and more.<br><blockquote>
  <b>I'll stay with you always; go where you go always. I don't want to be anywhere else. I couldn't stand to be anywhere else.</b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1388248059ra/7778584.gif" width="250" height="175" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I loved the whole <i>wild/animal</i> concept. It was interesting to see all kinds of characters thoughts on it. <br><b>
  <blockquote>You killed him like an animal would. I know that might not be a comfort to you now but the animal acts on instinct. An animal isn't evil, isn't good or bad.</blockquote>
</b><br><i>
  <blockquote>Wild is an interesting word. We imagine wild to be untamed and out of control but, of course, nature isn't like that; nature is controlled, ordered, extremely disciplined by all its elements.</blockquote>
</i><br>It was also very fascinating to see the thoughts of good vs evil by supposedly <i> the most evil Black Witch in history</i>. <br><b>
  <blockquote>The point of being good is doing it when it's tough, not when it's easy.</blockquote>
</b><br>Some people will always be prejudiced against. 'Half Wild' shows this clearly. It's the same for the society we live in today. Some people will always be judged for something their families did, or for their past. 'Half Wild' shows all of this from a fascinating angle. <i> I am looking forward to reading the third and final book in March 2016. *sigh* It seems so far away.</i><br><u>I recommend <i>'Half Wild'</i> to people who'd loved 'Half Bad' because then they'll surely love this one. Also, to people who'd like to see <i>good vs evil</i> concept being challenged by the the wild/animal concept.</u><br><br><i>I received an ARC of this novel thanks to the publisher via NetGalley in return for an honest review. My thanks for the opportunity.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="17822681408109511091" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText3267364427583944802" style="display:none">Ooh la la, new and beautiful cover there! <br /><br />Just some things I'm looking for in the next book:<br /><br />-More father son bonding. I thought it was, but then Nathan's dad shows up all mean and stuff, and I'm not so sure. But I think it'd be quite interesting if Nathan did have a dark side to him.   function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('daAUC6hk3eC2lSC5xO2e+2UJ9FF0zhJBgAxEo5IFuyVB6AOi02c6LUly8ApXn6rqmjg9mcHYAR6D1SiOLqG3pg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

He\'s short, he\'s fast, he\'s got a ton of potential—and he\'s the runaway son of the murderous crime lord known as The Butcher.\n\nSigning a contract with the PSU Foxes is the last thing a guy like Neil should do. <span id="freeTextContainer7802893057234474124">Hi - I'm Sally Green. I'm the author of the real-world/ fantasy Half Bad Trilogy, which is made up of Half Bad, Half Wild and Half Lost. Most people read them in that order but there's always a few who don't. Many people who read them are teenagers but there's a lot who aren't.<br/><br/>I'm currently working on a new series called The Smoke Thieves, which is due to be published in spring 2018 and is definit</span>
  <span id="freeText7802893057234474124" style="display:none">Hi - I'm Sally Green. I'm the author of the real-world/ fantasy Half Bad Trilogy, which is made up of Half Bad, Half Wild and Half Lost. Most people read them in that order but there's always a few who don't. Many people who read them are teenagers but there's a lot who aren't.<br /><br />I'm currently working on a new series called The Smoke Thieves, which is due to be published in spring 2018 and is definitely fantasy (there will be a map). <br /><br />I said I'd never write another trilogy after Half Bad but it seems I lied.<br /><br />I live in a village in north-west England.<br /><br />There's some stuff about the Half Bad trilogy at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.halfbadworld.com">www.halfbadworld.com</a>. <br /><br />Follow me on twitter@sa11eGreen <br /></span>
